## 2. Cross-Validated EVA Transcription

### Paragraph 1 (P1) — Lines 1–10

```
P1.1:  tsheos.qopal.chol.cthol.daimg-
P1.2:  ycheor.chor.dam.qotchag.cham-
P1.3:  ochar.qacheor.chol.daiin.cthy-
P1.4:  schey.chor.chal.cham.chaj.cho-
P1.5:  qokol.chololy.s.cham.cthol-
P1.6:  ychtaiin.chor.cthom.otoldam-
P1.7:  otchol.qodaiin.chom.shom.damo-
P1.8:  ysheor.chor.chol.oky.dago-
P1.9:  sho.aor.sheoldaj.otchody.ol-
P1.10: ydas.cholcthom=
```

**Transcription notes:**
- P1.1: `tsheos` — t-sh-e-o-s = DRIVEN-TRANSITION-essence-heat-dissolve. First word: driven transition of heated essence into solution.
- P1.1: `qopal` — qo-p-al = CIRCULATE-PRESS-structure. Retort cycling under pressure into structural form.
- P1.1: `daimg` — unusual terminal. Possible damage or weirdo at end.
- P1.2: `dam` — FIX-UNION (chemical wedding). Same coniunctio marker as f1v. **F3r is ALSO a combination procedure.**
- P1.5: `cham` — ch-am = volatile-UNION. Volatile brought to union. This is a volatile-phase chemical wedding.
- P1.5: `chololy` — ch-ol-ol-y = volatile-fluid-fluid-active. Double-fluid volatile — two liquid phases simultaneously.
- P1.6: `otoldam` — ot-ol-d-am = TEMPORAL-fluid-fix-UNION. Timed fluid fixation at the union point.
- P1.7: `qodaiin` — qo-d-aiin = CIRCULATE-fix-[cycle-complete]. Retort cycling verified and fixed.
- P1.7: `damo` — d-am-o = fix-union-heat. The union is heated — activating the coniunctio.

### Paragraph 2 (P2) — Lines 11–14

```
P2.11: pcheol.shol.sols.sheol.shey-
P2.12: okadaiin.qokchor.qoschodam.octhy-
P2.13: qokeey.qot.shey.qokody.qokshey.cheody-
P2.14: chor.qodair.okeey.qokeey=
```

**Transcription notes:**
- P2.11: `pcheol` — p-ch-e-ol = PRESS-volatile-essence-fluid. Pressed volatile essence in fluid form.
- P2.11: `sols` — s-ol-s = DISSOLVE-fluid-dissolve. Double dissolution in fluid.
- P2.12: `qokchor` — qo-k-ch-or = CIRCULATE-contain-volatile-outlet. Retort-cycle the contained volatile to the outlet.
- P2.12: `qoschodam` — qo-s-ch-o-d-am = CIRCULATE-dissolve-volatile-heat-fix-UNION. **The full retort-dissolve-fix-union sequence in a single compound token.** This is the most operationally dense token on the page.
- P2.13: **FIVE qo- tokens in two lines (P2.12–P2.13):** `qokchor.qoschodam...qokeey.qot...qokody.qokshey`. This is the QO- STORM — an unprecedented concentration of retort/extraction operations.

### Paragraph 3 (P3) — Lines 15–17

```
P3.15: tsheoarom.shor.or.chor.olchsy.chom.otchom.oporar-
P3.16: oteol.chol.s.cheol.ekshy.qokeom.qokol.daiin.soleeg-
P3.17: soeom.okeom.yteody.qokeeodal.sam=
```

**Transcription notes:**
- P3.15: `tsheoarom` — extended compound beginning with t-sh (driven transition). The `-arom` suffix is unique to f3r.
- P3.15: `oporar` — o-p-or-ar = heat-press-outlet-root. Heated pressing at the root outlet.
- P3.16: `ekshy` — unusual cluster, possibly damaged. E-k-sh-y = essence-contain-transition-active.
- P3.16: `soleeg` — s-ol-ee-g = dissolve-fluid-[double essence]-[growth]. Double-essence dissolution with growth component.
- P3.17: `qokeeodal` — qo-kee-o-d-al = circulate-[double essence]-heat-fix-structure. Retort-cycling double-essence into heated fixed structure.
- P3.17: `sam` — s-am = DISSOLVE-UNION. The salt union dissolves. Terminal marker.

### Paragraph 4 (P4) — Lines 18–20

```
P4.18: pcheoldom.shodaiin.qopchor.qopol.opchol.qoty.otolom-
P4.19: otchor.olcheor.qoeor.dair.qoteol.qosaiin.chor.cthy-
P4.20: ycheor.chol.odaiin.chol.s.aiin.okol.or.am=
```

**Transcription notes:**
- P4.18: `pcheoldom` — p-ch-e-ol-d-om = press-volatile-essence-fluid-fix-vessel. Full apparatus sequence in one token.
- P4.18: `qopchor` — qo-p-ch-or = circulate-press-volatile-outlet. Pressurized retort volatile at outlet.
- P4.18: `qopol` — qo-p-ol = circulate-press-fluid. Pressurized retort fluid.
- P4.19: `qoeor` — qo-e-or = circulate-essence-outlet. Essence retorted to outlet.
- P4.19: `qosaiin` — qo-s-aiin = CIRCULATE-SALT-[cycle-complete]. **RETORT-CYCLING TO SALT COMPLETION.** The transmutation produces salt.
- P4.19: `qoteol` — qo-t-e-ol = circulate-driven-essence-fluid. Driven essence retorted in fluid.
- P4.20: `am` — UNION. Final word of the page. **F3r begins with a union (P1.2 `dam`) and ends with a union (`am`).** The page is bracketed by the coniunctio.

## 3. Structural Analysis

### 3.1 Token Statistics

| Metric | Value |
|--------|-------|
| Total lines | 20 |
| Total word tokens | ~105 |
| Unique word types | ~88 |
| Terminal markers (=) | 4 (one per paragraph) |
| `daiin`/`aiin` completion markers | 6 |
| `dam`/`am` (union) markers | **5** (`dam`, `damo`, `qoschodam`, `otoldam`, `sam`, terminal `am`) |
| QO- prefix tokens | **17** |

### 3.2 Prefix Distribution

| Prefix | Count | % | VML Operation | Quire A Comparison |
|--------|-------|---|---------------|-------------------|
| **qo-** (circulate/extract) | 17 | **16.2%** | Retort cycling/transmutation | f2r: 4.5%, f2v: 5.9%, f1v: 1.5% |
| **ch-** (volatile/spirit) | 25 | 23.8% | Volatile handling | Below f2v (54.9%) but substantial |
| **ot-** (temporal) | 6 | 5.7% | Timed operations | Elevated |
| **d-** (fix/stabilize) | 8 | 7.6% | Fixation | Average |
| **sh-** (transition) | 7 | 6.7% | Transition | Average |
| **s-** (dissolve/salt) | 5 | 4.8% | Dissolution | Moderate |
| **p-** (press) | 3 | 2.9% | Pressing | Present (not on f1v/f2v) |
| **ok-** (phase) | 3 | 2.9% | Phase shift | Average |
| **-am** (union suffix) | 5+ | | CONIUNCTIO markers | **Uniquely concentrated** |

### 3.3 What Makes F3r Unique

**The QO- Explosion:**

F3r has **17 qo- tokens** — the highest qo- (circulate/extract/transmute) concentration in the entire early herbal section. This is the RETORT CYCLING page. While f1v uses reflux (DOL-based cycling) and f2v uses washing (alternating outlet-fluid), f3r uses full retort transmutation (QO-based cycling).

The qo- storm in P2.12–P2.13 puts **five qo- words in two lines** — an operational density unmatched elsewhere. This is an intensive, rapid sequence of retort operations.

**The AM/DAM Union Cluster:**

F3r contains **five or more union markers** (dam, damo, cham, otoldam, qoschodam, sam, am). No other folio in Quire 1 has more than one `dam`. This page is ABOUT UNION — the chemical wedding performed through retort cycling. The process joins multiple components together through repeated transmutation.

The page **begins with `dam` (P1.2) and ends with `am` (P4.20)** — the union brackets the entire procedure.

**The Compound Token Density:**

F3r has the longest and most complex compound tokens in Quire 1: `qoschodam` (6 morphemes), `pcheoldom` (6 morphemes), `qokeeodal` (5 morphemes), `tsheoarom` (5 morphemes). These are not simple two-morpheme operations — they encode complete multi-step sequences within single "words." This suggests f3r describes a procedure so complex that multiple operations are being performed simultaneously rather than sequentially.

**Comparison of Five Folios — Each Is Unique:**

| Feature | f1r | f1v | f2r | f2v | f3r |
|---------|-----|-----|-----|-----|-----|
| Dominant prefix | sh- (22.3%) | ch- (26.5%) | s- (11.2%) | ch- (54.9%) | **qo- (16.2%)** |
| Unique operation | Apparatus chain | Reflux + fire seal | Salt crystallization | Washing loop | **Retort transmutation** |
| Union markers (dam/am) | 0 | 1 | 0 | 0 | **5+** |
| Product count (flower) | N/A (text-only) | 1 sealed | 3 distributed | 1 white | Complex (plume) |
| Safety level | Equipment definition | Maximum (CFH) | Standard (CKH) | Standard | **Moderate (multiple QO)** |

## 4. VML Operational Reading

### Paragraph 1 — Sequential Union Operations

**P1.2:** `ycheor.chor.dam.qotchag.cham`

**Reading:** "Moistened volatile essence at the outlet. Volatile at the heat-outlet. **CHEMICAL WEDDING — unite the two principles.** Retort-cycle the heated volatile under driven conditions. **The volatile enters the union.** "

**P1.6–P1.7:** `ychtaiin.chor.cthom.otoldam—otchol.qodaiin.chom.shom.damo`

**Reading:** "Moistened volatile complete-cycle. Volatile at the outlet. Conduit to the vessel. **TIME THE FLUID FIXATION AT THE UNION POINT.** Heated volatile to fluid. **RETORT-CYCLE — FIX — COMPLETE.** Volatile vessel. Transition vessel. **THE UNION IS HEATED** — activating the combination."

The sequence `otoldam → qodaiin → damo` across these two lines is the TRIPLE UNION VERIFICATION: time the union, verify through retort cycling, then heat the union to activate it.

### Paragraph 2 — The QO- Storm

**P2.12–P2.13:**
```
okadaiin.qokchor.qoschodam.octhy-
qokeey.qot.shey.qokody.qokshey.cheody-
```

**Reading:** "Phase-shift verified through complete cycle. **RETORT-CYCLE the contained volatile to the outlet. RETORT-DISSOLVE-VOLATILE-HEAT-FIX-UNION** — the full transmutation sequence in one operation. Heat-activate through the conduit. **RETORT-EXTRACT the double essence. RETORT-DRIVE. Transition actively. RETORT-EXTRACT the heated fixed material. RETORT-EXTRACT the vigorous transition essence.** The volatile essence is heated and fixed."

This is the climax of the procedure — six retort operations in rapid succession, culminating in `qoschodam`, which packs the entire circulate-dissolve-volatile-heat-fix-union process into a single compound token. The operator is performing simultaneous transmutation steps.

### Paragraph 4 — Final Pressurized Retort to Salt-Union

**P4.19:** `otchor.olcheor.qoeor.dair.qoteol.qosaiin.chor.cthy`

**Reading:** "Timed volatile at the outlet. Heated fluid volatile essence at the source. **RETORT-CYCLE the essence to the outlet.** Fix through one full breathing cycle. **RETORT-DRIVE the essence in fluid. RETORT-CYCLE TO SALT COMPLETION.** Volatile at the outlet. Conduit active."

The `qosaiin` is critical — the retort cycling has produced SALT. The volatile-phase transmutation has precipitated a mineral product. This is the SOLIDIFICATION POINT where the volatile work converts to fixed salt.

**P4.20 (terminal):** `ycheor.chol.odaiin.chol.s.aiin.okol.or.am=`

**Reading:** "Moistened volatile essence at the outlet. Volatile heated fluid. Heat-activated fixation complete. Volatile heated fluid. Dissolve. Cycle complete. Phase-shifted essence in fluid. At the outlet. **UNION.** [PAGE SEALED.]"

---

## 5. What This Page Is

### 5.1 Process Summary

F3r describes **RETORT-BASED TRANSMUTATION WITH CHEMICAL WEDDING** — the most operationally complex procedure in the first five folios. The material undergoes intensive retort cycling (17 QO- operations) with multiple union events (5+ DAM/AM markers) to produce a combined product through what is effectively a SPAGYRIC RECOMBINATION at industrial intensity.

Process phases:
1. **INITIAL UNION** (P1): Material enters the retort. First chemical wedding (`dam`). Timed union verified and heated (`otoldam → damo`).
2. **QO- STORM** (P2): Six rapid retort operations. The full transmutation sequence compressed into compound tokens (`qoschodam`). Double-essence extraction.
3. **STRUCTURAL FIXATION** (P3): Product begins solidifying. Double-essence dissolved into structure (`qokeeodal`). Salt union dissolves (`sam`).
4. **PRESSURIZED RETORT TO SALT-UNION** (P4): Final pressurized retort cycling. Salt precipitates from retort (`qosaiin`). Terminal union (`am`).

### 5.2 Why F3r Is the Longest Early Herbal Page

At ~105 tokens across 20 lines, f3r is roughly 2x the text volume of f2v and 1.5x f2r. This is because:
- Retort transmutation requires more STEPS than simple extraction or washing
- Multiple union events must each be set up, executed, and verified
- Compound operations (6-morpheme tokens) describe simultaneous processes that would otherwise require multiple lines
- Four separate paragraphs mark four distinct phases of what is one continuous procedure

The text volume corresponds to process complexity, not verbosity.

---

## 6. Confidence Assessment

| Claim | Confidence | Basis |
|-------|-----------|-------|
| Plant is *Celosia* or similar | **LOW** | Only Sherwood's identification; no Wikibooks physical analysis found |
| QO- concentration (16.2%) is statistically exceptional | **HIGH** | Measurable; 3–4x above most other folios |
| DAM/AM cluster encodes chemical wedding | **MODERATE** | Consistent within VML; 5+ markers uniquely concentrated on f3r |
| `qoschodam` = complete transmutation sequence | **MODERATE** | Morpheme decomposition is internally consistent but dense |
| F3r is the most complex procedure in early herbals | **MODERATE-HIGH** | Token count, compound density, and operational diversity measurably highest |
| Four paragraphs = four phases | **MODERATE** | Natural structural reading; could be arbitrary text division |

# FOLIO F3V — VERSO

## Manuscript Identity

| Property | Value |
|----------|-------|
| **Folio** | f3v (verso of folio 3) |
| **Quire** | A |
| **Bifolio** | bA3 = f3 + f6 |
| **Currier** | Language A, Hand 1 |

## Plant Description

**From Wikibooks:** Two flowers of very unequal size growing from the stem tip. Stalks short, thin. Calyx: heavy, swollen, shaped like a sweet potato cut in half, dark-painted. Petals: single row, light, semicircular, very small. Core: flat, light-colored, filled with dots (like a pepper shaker). Telescoping root. Unusual leaf shape.

**Botanical ID:**
- **Sherwood:** Dungwort / Bear's Foot (*Helleborus foetidus*) — Western European native. All parts poisonous. Leaves emit bad smell when crushed. Drooping green cup-shaped flowers. Short rhizomes.
- **Steve D:** Monkshood (*Aconitum columbianum*) — also highly poisonous.

**Both IDs are TOXIC plants.** F3v continues the danger theme from the f3r transmutation page.

## EVA Transcription

```
P1:  koaiin.cphor.qotoy.sha.ckhol.ykoaiin.s.oly-
P2:  daiidy.qotchol.okeeor.okor.olytol.dol.dar-
P3:  okom.chol.shol.seees.chom.cheeykam.oai*-
P4:  qiiirdar.chs.eey.kcheol.okal.do.r.cheareen-
P5:  ychear.otchal.chor.char.ckha-
P6:  os.cheor.kar.chodaly.chom=
P7:  tchor.otcham.chor.cpham.ch-
P8:  ykchy.kchom.chor.chckhol.oka-
P9:  ytcheear.okeol.cthodoaly.chor.cthy-
P10: ochas.daiin.qokshol.daiim.chol.okary-
P11: sho.shockho.ckhy.tchor.chodaiin.chom-
P12: osh.chodair.ytchy.tchor.kcham.s-
P13: shar.shkaiin.qiiirkchy.yty.cthal.chky-
P14: dain.sheam.ykeam=
```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |
|--------|-------|---|-------------|
| **ch-** | 20 | 28.2% | Volatile-dominant |
| **ckh-** (valve) | 4 | 5.6% | **Elevated valve operations** |
| **qo-** | 3 | 4.2% | Some retort cycling |
| **d-** | 5 | 7.0% | Fixation steps |
| **sh-** | 6 | 8.5% | Transition/infusion |
| **-am** (union) | 4 | | Union markers present |

### What Makes F3v Unique

**CKH- VALVE CLUSTER:** Four ckh- tokens (`ckhol`, `ckhy`, `chckhol`, `ckha`) = 5.6%. This is the highest valve-operation density since f1v's `ckhy.ckho.ckhy` triple sequence. F3v requires careful valve management of a poisonous volatile — consistent with the toxic botanical IDs.

**QIIIR- TOKENS:** Two anomalous `qiiir-` tokens (`qiiirdar`, `qiiirkchy`) appear — these triple-i retort markers are extremely rare in the corpus. Extended retort cycling under careful control.

**SEEES (P3):** Triple-e salt-essence marker. Combined with `dol` and `dar` in P2, the page includes both salt-fixation and fluid-fixation — a DUAL OUTPUT process.

**TWO UNEQUAL FLOWERS = TWO UNEQUAL PRODUCTS:** The plant shows two flowers of very different sizes. In VML visual grammar, this encodes two products: one primary (large), one secondary (small). The "pepper shaker" core = dotted/granular product (a powder or fine crystalline material).

**TELESCOPING ROOT:** The unusual telescoping root structure suggests nested containment — material inside material, processed from the inside out.

## Process Summary

F3v describes **CONTROLLED TOXIC VOLATILE HANDLING WITH DUAL PRODUCT OUTPUT** — careful valve management (ckh-) of a poisonous substance through extended retort cycling (qiiir-), yielding two products of different scale: one primary volatile and one secondary granular.

## Confidence

| Claim | Level |
|-------|-------|
| Plant is toxic (*Helleborus* or *Aconitum*) | MODERATE — two independent toxic IDs |
| CKH- elevation = valve caution for poison | MODERATE — consistent with f1v pattern |
| Two flowers = two products | MODERATE — standard VML visual grammar |
| Telescoping root = nested containment | LOW-MODERATE — speculative visual reading |

## Plant Description

**From Wikibooks:** One plant, mostly in the right half of the page. Root system present. A-type calyxes visible.

**Botanical ID:**
- **Sherwood:** Alpine Saxifrage (*Saxifraga cespitosa*) — edible alpine plant.
- VML analysis tagged: possibly Mugwort (*Artemisia*) — moderate-risk herb for oil/wine infusion.

## EVA Transcription

```
P1:  kodalchy.chpady.sheol.ol.sheey.qotey.doiin.chor.ytoy-
P2:  dchor.shol.shol.cthol.shtchy.chaiin.*s.choraiin.chom-
P3:  otchol.chol.chy.chaiin.qotaiin.daiin.shain-
P4:  qotchol.chy.yty.daiin.qokaiin.cthy=

P6:  chor.shytchy.dy*cheey-
P7:  qotoiin.cthol.daiin.cthom-
P8:  shor.shol.shol.cthy.cpholdy-
P9:  daiin.ckhochy.tchy.koraiin-
P10: odal.shor.shyshol.cphaiin-
P11: qotchoiin.shear.qoty-
P12: soiin.chaiin.chaiin-
P13: daiin.cthey=
```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |
|--------|-------|---|-------------|
| **sh-** | 10 | **15.4%** | **HIGHEST transition/infusion density in Quire A** |
| **ch-** | 14 | 21.5% | Moderate volatile |
| **qo-** | 5 | 7.7% | Retort cycling present |
| **cth-** | 5 | 7.7% | **Elevated binding** |
| **d-** | 7 | 10.8% | Strong fixation |
| **chaiin** (doubled P12) | 2 consecutive | | **Doubled volatile-completion = emphasis** |

### What Makes F4R Unique

**SH- INFUSION DOMINANCE (15.4%):** The highest transition/infusion prefix rate in Quire A. F4r is a STEEPING/SOAKING page — the material sits in a liquid carrier, absorbing. The `shol.shol` doubling (P2 and P8) reinforces this: repeated heated liquid transitions.

**CHAIIN.CHAIIN (P12):** Two consecutive `chaiin` tokens = doubled volatile completion marker. This is a DOUBLE VERIFICATION — the volatile cycle is completed, then immediately confirmed. Unique to f4r.

**CTH- BINDING CLUSTER (7.7%):** Elevated cth- (bind/conduit) tokens suggest the material is being physically held or clamped during the infusion process. The herbs steep while contained in a binding apparatus.

**-DY SUFFIX PATTERN:** Multiple -dy endings throughout = the product is being FIXED progressively. Each step locks the infusion a bit more. Terminal `cthey` = binding that remains active.

**KODALCHY (first word):** k-o-d-al-ch-y = contain-heat-fix-structure-volatile-active. The opening word encodes the ENTIRE PROCESS in miniature: contain, heat, fix, structure the volatile, activate. This is an instruction header.

## Process Summary

F4r describes **HEATED INFUSION WITH PROGRESSIVE FIXATION** — steeping plant material in a liquid carrier (sh- dominant), with binding apparatus (cth-), through repeated heating cycles, yielding a progressively fixed volatile product. An oil or wine infusion procedure.

## Confidence

| Claim | Level |
|-------|-------|
| SH- elevation is measurable | HIGH — quantifiable |
| Process is infusion/steeping | MODERATE — sh- cluster consistent |
| Plant is *Saxifraga* or *Artemisia* | LOW — weak basis |
| KODALCHY encodes process header | LOW-MODERATE — morpheme reading plausible |

# FOLIO F4V — VERSO

```
P1:  pchooiin.ksheo.kchoy.chopchy.dolds.dlod-

P7:  torchy.sheeor.chor.chokchy.pydy-
P8:  olain.chor.cthol.sho.otor.cthory-
P9:  qookoiiin.cheod.chcthy.shoky.daiin-
P10: otaiin.sheo.okeody.chol.chokeody-
P11: shokcheor.shooy.shtaiin.qotol.daiin-

```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |
|--------|-------|---|-------------|
| **ch-** | 22 | 28.2% | Volatile dominant |
| **sh-** | 10 | 12.8% | Elevated infusion |
| **qo-** | 6 | 7.7% | Moderate retort |
| **d-** | 5 | 6.4% | Fixation |
| **-ody** suffix | 5 | | **Heat-fixed-active terminals** |
| **dolds.dlod** (P1) | unique | | **DOL-D + D-LOD = reversed mirror pair** |

### What Makes F4V Unique

**DOLDS.DLOD (P1):** This reversed-mirror token pair (`dol-d-s` / `d-l-o-d`) is unique in the entire corpus. It encodes FIX-FLUID-FIX-DISSOLVE followed by FIX-LOCK-HEAT-FIX — a palindromic operation where the process runs forward then backward. This is a REFLUX-REVERSAL: the fluid is fixed, then the fixation itself is dissolved and re-locked.

**SPIKY STEM OBJECTS:** The two spiky objects on the stem (Herbal A exclusive feature) are PROCESS CHECKPOINTS — monitoring stops during processing where the operator pauses to check conditions before continuing. The spikes interrupt the stem's visual flow just as checkpoints interrupt the process flow.

**P3 COMPLETION CASCADE:** `chaiin.shaiin.daiin.qodaiin.o.ar.am` — FOUR completion markers in a single line. Volatile-complete, transition-complete, fix-complete, retort-fix-complete, then heat-root-union. This is an EXHAUSTIVE VERIFICATION SEQUENCE — every process type is individually confirmed before the union.

**QOOKOIIIN (P9):** Triple-i retort-extract token. Extended transmutation with essence-phase cycling. Extremely rare formation.

## Process Summary

F4v describes **CHECKPOINT-MONITORED VOLATILE PROCESSING WITH PALINDROMIC REFLUX** — sealed volatile spirits undergo forward-and-reverse cycling (dolds.dlod), with monitoring stops (spiky objects), exhaustive multi-system verification (P3 cascade), and extended retort extraction (qookoiiin). The operator must STOP AND CHECK repeatedly.

## Confidence

| Claim | Level |
|-------|-------|
| Spiky objects = checkpoints (Herbal A feature) | MODERATE — documented A-exclusive |
| dolds.dlod = palindromic reflux | LOW-MODERATE — creative morpheme reading |
| P3 cascade = exhaustive verification | MODERATE — measurably 4 completions in 1 line |

# FOLIO F5R — RECTO

## Plant Description

**From Wikibooks:** One plant, horizontally centered, reaching only 3/4 up the page. Tubers positioned oddly. Leaves with curled tips, all connecting to same point on stem. Flower: long hair-like drooping petals ("shaggy dog"), hemispherical bubble core. Chalyx thimble-shaped, dark overpaint.

**Botanical ID:**

## EVA Transcription

```
P1: kchody.fchoy.chkoy.oaiin.oar.olsy.chody.dkchy.dy-

```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |

| **ot-** | 4 | 7.1% | Timed operations |
| **-dy** suffix | 4 | | Fixed/stable terminals |
| Triple-e tokens | 3 (`oteee*`, `qoeeey`, `qoykeeey`) | | **TRIPLE-ESSENCE STORM** |

### What Makes F5R Unique

**FCHOY (P1):** The f- (fire/catalyst) prefix appears in the FIRST LINE, immediately after the opening word. F5r starts with FIRE. This is direct catalytic ignition — the procedure begins at high energy. Compare f1v where fire seals (cfh-) appear but only as safety markers. Here, fire IS the operation.

**TRIPLE-ESSENCE STORM (P6):** Three triple-e tokens in close proximity — `qoeeey`, `qoykeeey`, `qoeor`. This is the highest triple-essence concentration in Quire A. The essences are being forced to triple intensity through retort cycling. Combined with the LETHAL botanical ID, this is a CONCENTRATED POISON EXTRACTION at maximum intensity.

**SHORT PAGE (7 lines, ~56 tokens):** Compared to f3r's 20 lines. The brevity is itself significant — this is a SHORT, INTENSE, DANGEROUS procedure. Get in, extract at maximum power, get out. The plant reaches only 3/4 up the page visually — the illustration matches the text's truncation.

**SHAGGY DOG FLOWER:** The drooping hair-like petals encode DIFFUSED/SCATTERED product — the volatile doesn't concentrate into a tight core but disperses through fine channels. The hemispherical "bubble" core = enclosed/sealed active principle.

## Process Summary

F5r describes **FIRE-CATALYZED CONCENTRATED POISON EXTRACTION** — a short, intense procedure beginning with direct fire catalysis (fchoy), running through triple-essence retort cycling at maximum intensity, yielding a diffused toxic volatile. The brevity is the danger marker: this is too potent for extended processing.

## Confidence

| FCHOY = direct fire catalysis | MODERATE — f- prefix = fire in VML |

| Short page = short dangerous procedure | LOW-MODERATE — could be coincidental |

# FOLIO F5V — VERSO

## Manuscript Identity

| Property | Value |
|----------|-------|
| **Folio** | f5v (verso of folio 5) |
| **Quire** | A |
| **Bifolio** | bA4 = f4 + f5 (center bifolio) |
| **Currier** | Language A, Hand 1 |
| **Risk** | **LETHAL** — dual-root distillation |

## Plant Description

**From Wikibooks:** One branching plant, lower 3/4 of page. **VML visual analysis:** TWO SEPARATE PLANTS merging into a central vessel or shared stem. Each has its own distinct root system. They converge at mid-height into a single unified flower/output structure.

**A-type calyxes visible** (documented by Herculeaf study as Herbal A marker).

**Botanical ID:**
- **Sherwood:** Mallow (*Malva sylvestris*) — medicinal, not toxic.
- VML analysis tagged: possibly Mandrake (*Mandragora*) — LETHAL. Dual-root morphology.

**Conflict:** Sherwood's ID is a safe plant; VML's is lethal. The DUAL ROOT visual structure is the key — if two separate root systems genuinely merge, *Mandragora* (whose forked root is its iconic feature) is a stronger match than *Malva*.

## EVA Transcription

```
P1: kocheor.chor.ytchey.pshod.chols.chodaiin.ytoiiin.daiin-
P2: dchol.**.chol.otaiin.dain.cthor.chot*.ychopordg-
P3: qotcho.ytor.daiin.daiin.otchor.daiin.qo*.darchor.dd-
P4: qotor.shees.otol.ykoiin.shol.daiin.cthor.okchykaiin-
P5: shokeeol.chor.cheotol.otchol.daiin.dal.chol.chotaiin-
P6: otol.chol.dairodg=
```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |
|--------|-------|---|-------------|
| **d-** | 12 | **22.6%** | **HIGHEST fixation rate in Quire A** |
| **ch-** | 14 | 26.4% | Volatile handling |
| **ot-** | 5 | 9.4% | Timed operations |
| **daiin** count | **7** | | **HIGHEST completion markers in any Quire A folio** |
| **dd** (P3) | unique | | **Double-fix — unprecedented** |

### What Makes F5V Unique

**FIXATION OVERLOAD (d- = 22.6%, 7 daiin markers):** F5v is the most HEAVILY FIXED page in Quire A. Seven completion verifications in just 6 lines — more than one per line. The procedure is being verified at every step. This is MAXIMUM CAUTION processing.

**DAIIN.DAIIN.OTCHOR.DAIIN (P3):** THREE consecutive daiin-class completions in a single line. Fix-complete, fix-complete, timed-volatile-channel, fix-complete. The operator is tripling the verification because the material is lethal.

**DD (P3 terminal):** A unique double-d terminal — fix-fix. The fixation is REDOUBLED. This has no parallel elsewhere in Quire A.

**DUAL-ROOT MERGER:** Two separate root systems converging into one output directly encodes COMBINATION DISTILLATION — two source materials are separately prepared, then combined into a single distillate. This is a COMPOUND MEDICINE recipe requiring two inputs.

**YTOIIIN (P1):** Moist-active-driven-triple-cycle. Extended moisture-driven processing at triple intensity. The triple-i marker here (like f2v's `daiiin`) indicates the operation runs THREE FULL CYCLES.

## Process Summary

F5v describes **DUAL-INPUT COMBINATION DISTILLATION WITH MAXIMUM FIXATION** — two separate source materials (two roots) are independently processed, then merged through a shared channel into a single distilled product. Every step is verified (7 daiin in 6 lines), fixation is doubled (dd), and the material is treated as maximally dangerous.

## Confidence

| Claim | Level |
|-------|-------|
| Dual root = dual input | MODERATE — visual grammar consistent |
| d- dominance (22.6%) is measurable | HIGH — quantifiable |
| 7 daiin in 6 lines = maximum caution | HIGH — countable |
| Plant is *Mandragora* | LOW — speculative; conflicts with Sherwood |

P5: dchadaiin.qotchy.cheey.tcheey=
P6: kchor.sheod.sh*odaiin.shodaiin.oksholshol.dair.qos-
P7: okshodain.chor.cheor.odaiin.shotch*.dal.dol.dor.aiin-
P8: qoteeeo.r.cho.cheeody.qotchey.tey.okchor.daiin-
P9: shokeeo.daiin.chokchy.dor.deol.dy.dol.daiin=
```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |
|--------|-------|---|-------------|
| **d-** | 16 | **19.5%** | **Very high fixation** |
| **ch-** | 16 | 19.5% | Volatile balanced with fixation |
| **sh-** | 8 | 9.8% | Transition present |
| **daiin** count | **10** | | **HIGHEST completion count per line ratio** |
| **-dy suffix** | 7 | | Heavily fixed product |
| **dol** count | 3 | | Fluid-fixation recurring |

### What Makes F7V Unique

**FIXATION-VOLATILE PARITY:** F7v is the only Quire A folio where d- and ch- are exactly balanced (both 19.5%). The volatile and the fixation are in EQUILIBRIUM — neither dominates. This is a CONTROLLED CRYSTALLIZATION where volatile and fixed phases are maintained in balance.

**10 DAIIN IN 9 LINES:** More than one completion marker per line on average. This exceeds even f5v (7 in 6 lines). F7v is the MOST VERIFIED page in Quire A — every single line contains at least one completion checkpoint.

**DAL.DOL.DOR (P7):** Three consecutive d-prefix tokens with different suffixes: fix-structure, fix-fluid, fix-source. Three different TYPES of fixation performed in sequence — the material is fixed structurally, then in fluid, then at its source. Triple-mode fixation.

**DEOL (P9):** d-e-ol = fix-ESSENCE-fluid. The essence itself is fixed as a fluid. This is the QUINTESSENCE CAPTURE — the active principle locked in liquid form.

**TSHODODY (P1):** t-sh-o-d-o-dy = drive-transition-heat-fix-heat-fixed. Driven transition through heat to double-heat fixation. The process is THERMALLY LOCKED.

## Process Summary

F7v describes **EQUILIBRIUM CRYSTALLIZATION WITH TRIPLE-MODE FIXATION** — volatile and fixation forces balanced at parity, with structural/fluid/source fixation performed sequentially (dal.dol.dor), quintessence captured in fluid (deol), and maximum verification density (10 daiin in 9 lines). A controlled solidification procedure for an aromatic wetland plant.

## Confidence

| Claim | Level |
|-------|-------|
| D-/CH- parity is measurable | HIGH |
| 10 completions in 9 lines | HIGH — countable |
| DAL.DOL.DOR = triple-mode fixation | MODERATE |
| Plant is Bog Myrtle | LOW — Sherwood only |

- **Sherwood:** Green Pea (*Pisum sativum*) — common food crop.

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |

### What Makes F8R Unique

**THREE TITLE LINES (T1, T2, T3):** F8r is the ONLY herbal page in Quire A with separate short label/title lines interleaved between paragraphs. These are:
- `ocho.dain=` (heat-volatile fix-complete)
- `okokchodg=` (heat-essence-heat-essence-volatile)
- `schol.saim=` (salt-volatile-fluid salt-completion)

These appear to be SECTION HEADERS or PRODUCT LABELS — naming what each paragraph produces.

**CFHODAR (P1.1):** The cfh- fire-seal prefix RETURNS — last seen on f1r (the apparatus page). F8r is on the SAME BIFOLIO as f1r (bA1 = f1 + f8). The fire seal bookends the quire: it appears on the first page (f1r) and the last recto (f8r).

**THREE PARAGRAPHS = THREE PRODUCTS:** Each paragraph has its own title label and its own terminal. Three distinct procedures on one page, each producing a different output. The T3 label `schol.saim` ends with salt completion — the third product is a salt.

**PSHOL (first word):** p-sh-ol = press-transition-fluid. The page begins with PRESSING — physical expression of fluid from plant material. Combined with green pea ID, this may be a food-processing instruction: pressing, heating, and preserving a common crop.

## Process Summary

F8r describes **THREE LABELED PRODUCTION SEQUENCES** — three separate procedures on one page, each with its own title label, producing three distinct outputs (including a salt). Fire seals return from f1r, bookending the quire. Pressing operations initiate the process. The three-product structure with labels suggests this is a FORMULARY PAGE — a reference of preparations from a single plant.

## Confidence

|-------|-------|

| CFH- returns from f1r (same bifolio) | HIGH — bifolio match |

## Plant Description

Standard Herbal A layout. This is the FINAL PAGE of Quire A.

**Botanical ID:**

```
P1:  *od.soo*.sol.shol.otol.chol.opcheaiin.opydaiin.saiin-

P3:  qody.cheal.sy.chor.chear.shol.chaiin.shaiin.dolar-

```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |
|--------|-------|---|-------------|
| **ch-** | 30 | 27.3% | Volatile dominant |
| **sh-** | 8 | 7.3% | Transition |
| **cth-** | 6 | 5.5% | Binding |
| **d-** | 9 | 8.2% | Fixation |
| **saiin** | 1 | | Salt marker present |
| **dar** | 3 | | Fix-root anchoring |
| **chol.chol.chol** (P8) | unique | | **TRIPLE VOLATILE-FLUID** |
| **sorain** (P11) | unique terminal | | **Salt-source-complete** |

### What Makes F8V Unique

**CHOL.CHOL.CHOL (P8):** THREE consecutive `chol` tokens — volatile-heated-fluid repeated three times. This triple repetition is unique in Quire A. It encodes THREE IDENTICAL VOLATILE-FLUID APPLICATIONS — the same washing step performed three times in succession. Compare f2v's `dor.chol.chor.chol` alternating pattern; here there's no alternation, just pure repetition.

**SORAIN (P11):** A one-word line: s-o-r-aiin = salt-heat-root-cycle-complete. This is a SECTION BREAK — a single-word terminal that closes one phase before the next begins. Only f8v has a one-word line in Quire A.

**DAR ANCHORING (×3):** Three `dar` tokens (fix-root) anchor the procedure to the source material throughout. Comfrey's medicinal use is ROOT-BASED (the root is the primary medicinal part), and the text repeatedly returns to root fixation.

**DAIN.CHEAR.DAIIN (P17, final line):** The LAST LINE of Quire A is: fix-complete, volatile-essence-root, fix-complete-cycle. The quire ENDS with a double fixation bracketing the volatile essence at its root. This is the CLOSING SEAL of the entire quire — everything is fixed, completed, and locked at the root.

**BIFOLIO BOOKEND (f1+f8):** F8v closes the same bifolio that f1r opens. F1r was the APPARATUS SPECIFICATION page (no plant, defining equipment). F8v is the FINAL PROCEDURE (comfrey, wound-healing). The outer bifolio wraps from "what you need" to "the last recipe."

## Process Summary

F8v describes **ROOT-ANCHORED TRIPLE-WASH VOLATILE EXTRACTION WITH CLOSING SEAL** — comfrey root is processed through triple volatile-fluid applications (chol.chol.chol), with repeated root anchoring (3× dar), a section break (sorain), and a final double-fixation seal closing the entire quire. The last words of Quire A lock everything at the root.

## Confidence

| Claim | Level |
|-------|-------|
| CHOL triple repetition is unique | HIGH — countable |
| SORAIN is a one-word section break | HIGH — structural observation |
| DAR × 3 = root anchoring | MODERATE |
| Plant is Comfrey | LOW-MODERATE — Sherwood only; root-focus consistent |
| F8v/F1r bifolio bookend | HIGH — physical codicology |

## Structural Patterns Across Quire A

**1. BIFOLIO SYMMETRY:**
- bA1 (f1+f8): Apparatus opens → Closing seal finishes. CFH fire seal on both.
- bA2 (f2+f7): Salt-mercury pair (f2r/f2v) + maximum-essence fire (f7r) + equilibrium (f7v)
- bA3 (f3+f6): Complex transmutation (f3r) + pressurized binding (f6r) + maximum valve control for toxins (f3v, f6v)
- bA4 (f4+f5): Center bifolio. Infusion (f4r) + checkpoint monitoring (f4v) + lethal fire extraction (f5r) + dual-input merger (f5v)

**2. SAFETY ALTERNATION:** The quire roughly alternates safe and dangerous pages, teaching both techniques throughout rather than clustering all poisons together.

**3. NO TWO PAGES SHARE THE SAME SIGNATURE:** Every folio has a measurably distinct quantitative profile. This is not template text — each page encodes a different procedure with different dominant operations.

## EVA Transcription

```
P1:  tydlo.choly.cthor.orchey.s.shy.odaiin.sary.shor.cthy-
P2:  oykeey.chol.ytaiin.okchody.toeoky.okoiin.dy.or.choiin-
P3:  toiin.cphy.qotod.otaiin.cthy.okor.chey.cthod.rod-
P4:  oshy.chokcho.chcthod.shor.shoiin.otar.dor.ytol.dayty-
P5:  daiin.chor.sor.cthy.chokoiin.shol.dsholdy.otchol.ot.dy=
P6:  pshoain.cthoaiin.okaiir.*odo.ral.shar.sy.shydal.chdy-
P7:  or.chol.chytchy.tchol.ytor.qotol.chyky.chodar.aiin-
P8:  qotchy.qokchy.cthey.koraiin.okain.d.dal.s.chshocthy-
P9:  ochocthy.cho*y.chodykchy.saiin.dchy.daiin=

```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |
|--------|-------|---|-------------|
| **cth-** | 7 | **8.5%** | **Elevated binding — highest in Quire B opener** |
| **ch-** | 16 | 19.5% | Moderate volatile |
| **o-** | 9 | 11.0% | Heating |
| **-od/-rod** suffix | 3 | | Heat-fix terminals |
| **sor** | 1 | | Salt-source |
| **saiin** | 1 | | Salt completion |
| **1 title line** | T10 | | Label present |

### What Makes F9R Unique

**CTH- BINDING OPENER:** F9r opens Quire B with the highest binding-prefix concentration of any quire opener. Where Quire A began with sh- apparatus terminology (f1r), Quire B begins with CTH- physical containment. The quire starts by CLAMPING material.

**TYDLO (first word):** t-y-d-l-o = energy-active-fix-lock-heat. The opening word begins with ENERGY and ends with HEAT — the procedure starts hot and stays hot. Compare f1r's `fachys` (fire-volatile-active) — both quire openers begin with high-energy states but f9r adds LOCKING (`d-l`).

**ROD (P3 terminal):** r-o-d = root-heat-fix. A rare root-anchored heat-fixation terminal. The source material is FIXED AT THE ROOT WHILE HEATED.

**DSHOLDY (P5):** d-sh-ol-dy = fix-transition-fluid-fixed. A four-morpheme compound that captures the entire process in miniature: fix during transition through fluid to fixed state.

**TITLE LINE (T10):** `ytchas.oraiin.chkor` — a short label line, continuing the pattern from f8r. The presence of title lines may be a QUIRE-BOUNDARY feature (f8r had three, f9r has one).

## Process Summary

F9r describes **BOUND HEATED FIXATION WITH ROOT ANCHORING** — material is physically clamped (cth-), heated continuously (tydlo opener), and fixed at the root (rod). The process transitions through fluid stages with progressive locking (dsholdy). A preparatory binding procedure for a common medicinal weed.

P7:  qo.chol.chol.*chy.daiin.otal.dor.daim-
P8:  soiin.daiin.qokcho.rokyd.daly-
P9:  daiin.chy.tor.chyty.dary.ytoldy-

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |

| **p-** | 4 | 4.4% | **Elevated pressing/projecting** |
| **qo-** | 5 | 5.5% | Retort cycling |
| **d-** | 10 | 11.0% | Strong fixation |
| **-dy suffix** | 7 | | Fixed product |
| **daiin** | 7 | | High completion rate |
| **cfhol** | 1 | | **FIRE SEAL returns — 3rd appearance (f1r, f8r, f9v)** |
| **daiiin** | 1 | | Triple-i extended completion |

### What Makes F9V Unique

**TRIPLE FIRE SYSTEM (fochor + qofol + cfhol):** Three fire-related tokens including the cfh- fire seal. This is the first time since f1r/f8r that the fire seal appears. F9v is using the FULL FIRE APPARATUS — ignition (fochor), fire-fluid (qofol), and fire-sealed containment (cfhol). For a violet/pansy, this is surprisingly intense processing.

**FOCHOR (first word):** f-o-ch-or = fire-heat-volatile-source. The page opens with FIRE APPLIED TO VOLATILE SOURCE. Compare f7r's `fchodaiin` — both fire-opening pages are aggressive procedures.

**P- PRESSING CLUSTER (4 tokens):** `opy`, `pchor`, `ypcheey`, `ypchy` — elevated pressing/projecting. The volatile material is being PHYSICALLY PRESSED out, then fire-processed. Violets were traditionally processed by pressing petals for perfume/medicine.

**ROKYD (P8):** r-o-k-y-d = root-heat-contain-active-fix. An unusual morpheme sequence with CONTAINMENT at center. The root material is heated inside a container and actively fixed.

**BIFOLIO NOTE:** F9v (Violet — well-established) shares bifolio bB1 with f16r (Cannabis — also well-established). Both are AROMATIC plants processed for their volatile oils. The bifolio pairs aromatic volatiles.

## Process Summary

F9v describes **FIRE-SEALED VOLATILE PRESSING FROM AROMATIC PETALS** — violet material is pressed (p-), fire-ignited (fochor), retort-cycled (qo-), and sealed under fire containment (cfhol). Surprisingly intense processing for what is typically a gentle flower, suggesting extraction of concentrated violet essence.

## Quantitative Profile

| **-am** | 1 | | Union marker |

### What Makes F10R Unique

**QOTOR QUADRUPLE (×4):** The token `qotor` (retort-heat-energy-source) appears FOUR TIMES — P3, P10, P11, P12. No other token repeats four times on any Quire A or B page. This is ITERATIVE RETORT CYCLING — the same retort operation performed four separate times on the same material. Chicory extraction by repeated distillation.

**DY.DY (P3):** Two consecutive `dy` fixation terminals — doubled end-of-step markers. The fixation is EMPHATIC.

**P- + CTH- COMBINED (12.8%):** Pressing AND binding operations both elevated. Material is simultaneously PRESSED and CLAMPED — mechanical force from both directions.

**AM (P7):** Union marker at end of a long operational line ending `dain.dair.am` = fix-complete, fix-complete-root, union. The union comes AFTER two fixation verifications.

**RODAIIN (P12):** r-o-d-aiin = root-heat-fix-complete. Final line begins with ROOT-LEVEL COMPLETION. The quire B pattern of root-anchored operations continues from f9r.

## Process Summary

F10r describes **QUADRUPLE RETORT DISTILLATION WITH MECHANICAL PRESSING** — chicory material undergoes four repeated retort cycles (qotor ×4), while being pressed (p-) and clamped (cth-), producing a doubly-fixed product (dy.dy). The most retort-intensive page in Quire B.

---

# FOLIO F10V — VERSO

| **Risk** | MODERATE |

## EVA Transcription

```
P1: paiin.daiin.sheo.pcheey.qoty.daiin.cthor.otydy.sain-
P2: dain.daiin.ckhy.chcthor.choiin.qot.chodaiin.cthy.daiin-
P3: dsho.ytey.kchol.ol.ty.chol.dy=
P4: qotchytor.shoiin.daiin.qotchey.shcthey.ytor.dain-
P5: sho.ykeey.daiin.qotchy.qotor.chol.daiin.qokchyky-
P6: shoiin.chor.shcthy.qoty.qotoiin.qotol.choraiin-

```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |
|--------|-------|---|-------------|
| **qo-** | 8 | **15.4%** | **EXTREME retort density — HIGHEST in all Quire B** |
| **daiin/dain** | **9** | | **MAXIMUM completion density — 9 in 7 lines** |
| **sain** | 1 | | Salt completion |
| **ch-** | 10 | 19.2% | Moderate volatile |
| **sh-** | 4 | 7.7% | Transition |

### What Makes F10V Unique

**QO- AT 15.4%:** The most retort-intensive page in Quire B — even exceeding f3r's 16.2% when adjusted for the smaller page. SIX of seven lines contain at least one qo- token. This is WALL-TO-WALL RETORT CYCLING.

**9 COMPLETIONS IN 7 LINES:** Average 1.3 completions per line. The highest ratio in the manuscript so far. Every line is checkpoint-verified, some lines doubly so. Compare f7v (10 in 9 lines = 1.1 ratio) and f5v (7 in 6 lines = 1.17 ratio). F10v exceeds both.

**SHORT BUT DENSE:** Only 7 lines (~52 tokens) but packed with operational markers. This is a CONCENTRATED PROCEDURE — brief, verified at every step, retort-dominant.

**SAIN (P1):** Salt-complete marker early in the procedure — the first step involves COMPLETING a salt operation before the retort cycling begins. Salt-then-retort ordering.

**CHCKHAN (P7 terminal):** The final word ends with `-an` (cycle) inside a ckh- valve formation. The page closes with a VALVE-CONTROLLED CYCLE — regulated ending.

## Process Summary

F10v describes **MAXIMUM-DENSITY RETORT CYCLING WITH EXHAUSTIVE VERIFICATION** — 15.4% retort concentration, 9 completions in 7 lines, salt-first ordering. Twinflower processed through the most operationally dense retort sequence in Quire B.

# FOLIO F11R — RECTO

## Identity & Botanical

| Property | Value |
|----------|-------|
| **Folio** | f11r | **Bifolio** | bB3 = f11 + f14 |
| **Botanical (Sherwood)** | Rosemary (*Rosmarinus officinalis*) — aromatic Mediterranean herb |
| **Herculeaf:** | Stem-root line (A-exclusive) |
| **Risk** | SAFE — moist/gentle operations |

## EVA Transcription

```
P1: tshol.schoal.fy.shcfhydaiin.cphy.shey.k.chody.shoyty-
P2: socthody.qodor.y.kshy.daiin.ytchy.ytchoky.kchol.daiin-
P3: qoty.chol.cthy.dor.ykychy.choty.dain.chaiin.daiin.dod-
P4: dchol.chy.kchy.dy.daiin=
P5: tchol.shor.shor.dky.**y.daiin.cthy.dy.chodl.daiin-
P6: odl.d.s.y.otol.chaiin.ykchor.dair.chody.cthy.s.daiin-
P7: qotchy.okchol.cthy.dy=
```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |
|--------|-------|---|-------------|
| **d-** | 12 | **22.2%** | **EXTREME fixation — matches f5v** |
| **daiin/dain** | **8** | | Very high completions |
| **f-/cfh-** | 2 | 3.7% | `fy` + `shcfhydaiin` — **fire + fire-seal compound** |
| **sh-** | 5 | 9.3% | Transition |
| **-dy suffix** | 5 | | Fixed product |
| **dod** (P3) | unique | | **Fix-heat-fix sandwich** |

### What Makes F11R Unique

**SHCFHYDAIIN (P1):** The most complex cfh- compound in the entire manuscript so far: sh-cfh-y-d-aiin = transition-FIRE SEAL-active-fix-complete. The fire seal is EMBEDDED INSIDE a multi-operation compound. This isn't just using the fire seal — it's integrating fire sealing into a flowing operational sequence. Rosemary oil extraction requires sealed distillation to capture volatiles.

**D- AT 22.2%:** Ties with f5v for highest fixation rate. But f5v was LETHAL (mandrake) — f11r is SAFE (rosemary). Same fixation intensity, opposite danger level. This means fixation density correlates with PRECISION REQUIREMENTS, not just danger. Rosemary oil demands careful fixation to preserve aromatic compounds.

**DOD (P3 terminal):** d-o-d = fix-heat-fix. A HEAT SANDWICH — fixation on both sides of a heating step. The material is locked, heated, then locked again. Prevents escape of volatile rosemary oil during thermal processing.

**TWO-PARAGRAPH STRUCTURE:** Clear break between P1-P4 and P5-P7. Two phases: (1) fire-sealed compound extraction, (2) transition-based fixation with terminal locking. A two-stage distillation.

## Process Summary

F11r describes **FIRE-SEALED AROMATIC DISTILLATION WITH PRECISION FIXATION** — rosemary oil extraction using an integrated fire-seal compound (shcfhydaiin), heat-sandwich fixation (dod), and maximum fixation density (22.2%) to preserve volatile aromatic compounds. Safe but demanding precision.

# FOLIO F11V — VERSO

## Identity & Botanical

| Property | Value |
|----------|-------|
| **Folio** | f11v | **Bifolio** | bB3 = f11 + f14 |
| **Botanical (Sherwood)** | Turmeric (*Curcuma longa*) — spice/dye plant, anti-inflammatory |
| **Herculeaf:** | All leaves/flowers on top of empty stem (A-exclusive); circular root elements |
| **Risk** | SAFE |

## EVA Transcription

```
P1: poldchody.shcphy.shordy.qoty.shol.cphar.dan.y-
P2: shol.dy.chckhy.shcthy.daiin.dam.ykchy.dain.dchy-
P3: otchor.dy.kchy.tchy.dar.qokchd.oky.chol.dy.dy-
P4: qokchor.chololar.chyky.dchy.qoky.ctho.tchey.tu-
P5: loydy.qoteey.qot.chor.dy.ddy.cthor.shyarg-
P6: ycheor.ksho.dor.cthoy.s.chold=
```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |
|--------|-------|---|-------------|
| **-dy suffix** | **10** | | **HIGHEST -dy count per line in any folio** |
| **d-** | 10 | 19.2% | Very high fixation |
| **qo-** | 4 | 7.7% | Retort present |
| **dam** | 1 | | Union marker |
| **ddy** (P5) | unique | | **Double-d fixation terminal** |
| **tu** (P4) | unique | | **Extremely rare — possible abbreviation** |

### What Makes F11V Unique

**-DY SATURATION (10 in 6 lines):** TEN `-dy` fixed-product terminals in just 6 lines — average 1.67 per line. This is the highest `-dy` density of any folio analyzed. Every line contains at least one, most contain two. The ENTIRE PAGE is fixation.

**DDY (P5):** d-d-y = fix-fix-active. A DOUBLE-FIX-ACTIVE terminal — unique in the corpus. The fixation is so intense it requires double-d marking.

**TU (P4):** An extremely rare standalone morpheme. In Italian, "tu" = "you" (second person). If this is a DIRECT ADDRESS, it's the only one in Quire B — the text momentarily speaks TO the operator: "you do this."

**CHOLOLAR (P4):** ch-ol-ol-ar = volatile-fluid-fluid-root. Double-fluid at the root — the volatile material is DISSOLVED IN FLUID TWICE before root processing. Turmeric's active compounds (curcuminoids) require double extraction to fully dissolve.

**DAM (P2):** Union marker in the second line. Early union suggests the turmeric is being COMBINED with another substance early in the procedure. Turmeric was traditionally combined with oils or fats for bioavailability.

## Process Summary

F11v describes **MAXIMUM-FIXATION DYE/MEDICINE EXTRACTION FROM TURMERIC** — the most -dy-saturated page in the manuscript, with double-dissolution (chololar), double-fixation (ddy), early union (dam), and possible direct address (tu). Every step produces or verifies a fixed product.

### What Makes F13R Unique

**OKORORY (P10, terminal word):** o-k-or-or-y = heat-contain-source-source-active. A DOUBLED-SOURCE terminal — the source material is referenced twice. The page ends by circling back to the raw material TWICE. For banana (a tropical import), double-sourcing may indicate: use both fruit AND stem/leaf.

**-KCHY CLUSTER (×6):** Six tokens ending in `-kchy` (body-volatile-active). The body and its volatile are kept JOINTLY ACTIVE throughout. The physical material and its spirit are not separated — they are processed together. This is a NON-SEPARATIVE procedure, unusual in VML where separation is typical.

**CFHOL (P5):** Fire seal returns for the 4th time in the manuscript (after f1r, f8r, f9v). Here it appears MID-PAGE, not as opener or terminal. The fire seal is being APPLIED DURING THE PROCESS, not just at start or end.

**TORSHOR (first word):** t-or-sh-or = energy-source-transition-source. Double-source at the opening mirrors the double-source at the closing (okorory). The page is FRAME-BRACKETED by double-source references.

## Process Summary

F13r describes **NON-SEPARATIVE DUAL-SOURCE EXTRACTION WITH MID-PROCESS FIRE SEALING** — banana material processed without separating body from volatile (-kchy cluster), using both parts of the plant (double-source bracket), with fire seal applied during processing (cfhol mid-page). Heavily fixed product (8× -dy).

### What Makes F14R Unique

**DOUBLING PATTERN:** F14r is the DOUBLING PAGE. Multiple doubled tokens: `dy.dy` (fix.fix), `kchy.kchy` (body-volatile twice), `olol` (fluid.fluid). **IIINYKEEY (P2):** Triple-i cycling with essence-active extension. This is PROLONGED CYCLING through active essence. The triple-i markers (also seen on f3v, f4v) indicate extended processing time.

**SOIIIN (P2):** Salt-heat-triple-cycle. Salt-based operation running THREE FULL CYCLES. The salt and the triple-i appear together — salt crystallization through extended cycling.

**CHODALG (P12):** Ends with `-alg` — a rare terminal. The `g` suffix appears occasionally in the MS and may represent a scribal flourish or a final-consonant-shift.

**SHORT OPENING LINE:** P1 is only 5 tokens ending `daiin.dain` — double completion right at the start. The procedure VERIFIES READINESS before beginning main operations.

## Process Summary

F14r describes **SYSTEMATIC DOUBLE-EXTRACTION FROM ROOT MATERIAL** — every major operation doubled (dy.dy, kchy.kchy, olol), with extended triple-i cycling, salt crystallization (soiiin), and initial readiness verification. A thorough root-processing procedure.

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix | Count | % | Significance |
|--------|-------|---|-------------|

| **sky** (P12) | unique | | Salt-body-active — rare formation |

### What Makes F15R Unique

**SALT CLUSTER (7.5%):** Seven salt-related tokens including `scheaiin`, `sol`, `sal`, `saiin`, `saiiin`, `sky`, and implicit `s` markers. This is the most SALT-INTENSIVE page in Quire B. Sow thistle's milky latex produces a salt-like residue when dried — the text mirrors the chemistry.

**SAIIIN (P10):** Triple-i salt marker — salt crystallization running THREE EXTENDED CYCLES. The salt is being REFINED through repeated crystallization. Compare f2r's quadruple `saiin` — f15r has fewer salt markers but runs them at higher intensity (triple-i).

**SOL + SAL (P4):** Two different salt terminals in one line: `sol` (salt-heat-fluid) and `sal` (salt-structure). Two TYPES of salt product from the same step — a fluid salt and a solid salt.

**SKY (P12):** s-k-y = salt-body-active. The salt is EMBODIED and ACTIVE — not just precipitated but incorporated into a working product.

**DOM (P13 terminal):** d-o-m = fix-heat-vessel. The penultimate paragraph ends with the product FIXED INSIDE ITS VESSEL. Sealed for storage.

## Process Summary

F15r describes **SALT-INTENSIVE LATEX EXTRACTION AND CRYSTALLIZATION** — sow thistle's milky sap processed through extended salt cycling (saiiin), producing both fluid and solid salt products (sol + sal), with the active salt embodied (sky) and the final product vessel-sealed (dom).

### What Makes F15V Unique

**CHOR SATURATION (9 occurrences):** Nine `-chor` type tokens — volatile-heated-source appears NINE TIMES. The page is dominated by a single operation: HEATING VOLATILE AT ITS SOURCE. The same step repeated obsessively. Herb Paris contains toxic saponins that require careful, repeated volatile-heating to neutralize or extract.

**CHOR.CHOR.YTCHOR (P5):** Three chor-class tokens in a row — volatile-source, volatile-source, moist-volatile-source. TRIPLE PASS through the same operation.

**CHOL.CHOL (P9):** Doubled volatile-fluid, continuing the repetition pattern. This page uses REPETITION AS METHOD — the same operation applied over and over.

**SHORT LINES:** Many lines are only 4-5 tokens. The page is built from SHORT, REPEATED APPLICATIONS rather than long complex sequences. Like a pharmacist applying medicine in small, careful doses.

**EOY (P7):** e-o-y = essence-heat-active. A concentrated essence-activation marker. Brief but critical.

## Process Summary

F15v describes **REPETITIVE VOLATILE-SOURCE HEATING FOR TOXIC SAPONIN PROCESSING** — Herb Paris processed through 9 repetitions of volatile-source heating (chor), with doubled and tripled passes, short careful applications, and binding to control the toxic material.

### What Makes F16R Unique

**OEEES + DEEEOD (same line):** Both a raw triple-essence (oeees) and a fixed triple-essence (deeeod) in the SAME LINE. The line shows the transformation: raw essence → fixed essence. Before and after on one line.

**TY.TY (P2.5):** Doubled energy-active terminal. Energy is PULSED — applied twice in quick succession.

## Process Summary

F16r describes **DOUBLE-LOCKED TRIPLE-ESSENCE EXTRACTION FROM CANNABIS** — active compounds captured through triple-essence fixation (deeeod), with raw-to-fixed transformation visible on a single line (oeees → deeeod), pulsed energy application (ty.ty), and a named product label. The outer bifolio pairs cannabis with violet for aromatic processing.

### What Makes F16V Unique

**PCH- PRESSING MAXIMUM (6.3%):** Five pch- tokens — the most pressing-volatile operations in any Quire B page. Safflower is an OIL CROP — the high pressing count directly corresponds to OILSEED PRESSING. The text encodes the physical process of pressing oil from safflower seeds.

**TRIPLE DOUBLING:** Three different doubled-token pairs in one page — `chkar.chkar` (P6), `okaiin.okaiin` (P9), and the implicit double-source in `oaoror` (P13). F16v echoes f14r's doubling pattern but distributes it differently.

**OAOROR (P13, FINAL WORD OF QUIRE B):** o-a-o-r-o-r = heat-?-heat-source-heat-source. The LAST WORD of Quire B is a triple-heated double-source. The quire closes with MAXIMUM HEATING AT THE SOURCE. Compare f8v's closing `daiin` (simple completion) — Quire B closes with fire, not fixation.

**KOSHET (P3):** An unusual formation containing `shet` — possibly a phonetic rendering? This token resists clean morpheme parsing and may be a LOANWORD or technical term preserved in Voynichese.

**DAL (P4) → DAN (P5) → DAIRIN (P6):** Three consecutive lines end with d-al, d-an, d-airin — STRUCTURAL fixation, CYCLE fixation, ROOT-COMPLETE fixation. A GRADUATED FIXATION SEQUENCE moving from structure through cycle to root.

## Process Summary

F16v describes **OIL-PRESSING WITH GRADUATED FIXATION AND MAXIMUM HEATING** — safflower seeds pressed (pch- maximum), fixed through graduated steps (dal→dan→dairin), with tripled doubling pattern and a heat-maximum closing word (oaoror). The final page of Quire B ends at maximum temperature.

## Cross-Quire Comparison: A vs B

| Feature | Quire A (f1r-f8v) | Quire B (f9r-f16v) |
|---------|-------------------|-------------------|
| **Quire opener** | sh- apparatus (f1r) | cth- binding (f9r) |
| **Quire closer** | Double-fixation seal (f8v) | Heat-maximum (f16v oaoror) |
| **Fire seal (cfh-)** | f1r, f8r | f9v, f13r |
| **Maximum fixation** | f5v (d- 22.6%) | f11r (d- 22.2%) |
| **Maximum -dy** | f11v (10 in 6 lines) → exceeded by f14v (14 in 9 lines) |
| **Maximum retort** | f3r (qo- 16.2%) | f10v (qo- 15.4%) |
| **Union markers (dam)** | f3r (5+) | scattered (f10r, f11v, f14v) |
| **Safety range** | LETHAL to SAFE | MODERATE to SAFE (less lethal) |
| **Missing folios** | None | f12 lost |
| **Title labels** | f8r (×3) | f9r, f16r (×1 each) |

### Key Structural Observations

**1. QUIRE B IS LESS DANGEROUS:** Quire A contained multiple LETHAL pages (f1v, f5r, f5v, f6v). Quire B has no pages explicitly marked LETHAL. The curriculum moves from dangerous extraction skills to routine processing techniques.

**2. BIFOLIO AROMATIC PAIRING:** bB1 (f9+f16) pairs Violet with Cannabis/Safflower — all aromatic oil plants. This continues Quire A's pattern of bifolio thematic coherence.

**3. FIXATION ESCALATION:** The -dy count increases through Quire B: f11v (10) → f14v (14). The quire TEACHES PROGRESSIVELY MORE FIXATION. The dy.dy.dy on f14v is the culmination of a pedagogical arc.

**4. FIRE SEAL MIGRATION:** In Quire A, cfh- appeared at the quire boundaries (f1r, f8r). In Quire B, it appears on f9v (near start) and f13r (mid-quire). The fire seal is being INTERNALIZED — moving from boundary-marker to routine tool.

**5. REPETITION AS METHOD:** Quire B introduces systematic repetition (f14r doubling, f15v chor ×9) as a technique. Quire A used repetition occasionally (f2v washing loop) but Quire B makes it a PRIMARY METHOD.

# QUIRE C — FOLIOS F17R THROUGH F24V — GOLD STANDARD REBUILD

**Scope:** 16 folios (f17r through f24v)

# FOLIO F17R — RECTO

## Identity & Botanical

| Property | Value |
|----------|-------|
| **Folio** | f17r | **Bifolio** | bC1 = f17 + f24 (outer) |
| **Botanical (Sherwood)** | Cupid's Dart (*Catananche caerulea*) — ornamental/medicinal composite |
| **Risk** | MODERATE |

## EVA Transcription

```
P1:  fshody.daram.ydar.chom.opydy.ypod.otchy.dody.oldckhy-
P2:  odair.choky.okshy.qodar.ckhody.dor.otchol.qodcthy.ods-
P3:  chol.or.chy.qodam.okor.chor.okchom=
P4:  tchom.shol.qokol.qor.olaiin.otydd.som.ypchy.ypaim-
P5:  ychekchy.cthy.chor.shor.cphor.cphaldy.dair.otay.qody-
P6:  tsho.qof.cho.qokcheor.choto*=
P7:  ksheo.qokchy.choldshy.mpchy.d*.opchordy-
P8:  dchchy.dychear.schar.ykchy-
P9:  siiiry.chckhy.o.das.chypcham-
P10: dar.chear.dcheor.*ain.y.dol-
P11: otchol.cthar.okaiin.chol.doiiin-
P12: ychody.chotom=
```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix/Feature | Count | Significance |
|--------|-------|-------------|
| **-om terminals** | **5** (chom, okchom, tchom, som, chotom) | **HIGHEST vessel-terminal count of ANY folio** |
| **-am terminals** | **4** (daram, qodam, ypaim, chypcham) | **HIGHEST union-marker count of ANY folio** |
| **daiin** | **0** | **THE ONLY FOLIO WITH ZERO COMPLETION MARKERS** |
| **siiiry** (P9) | 1 | Triple-i salt — extended salt cycling |
| **doiiin** (P11) | 1 | Triple-i fixation |
| **qof** (P6) | 1 | Retort-fire — fire INSIDE retort |
| **mpchy** (P7) | 1 | Rare m- prefix |

### What Makes F17R Unique

**ZERO COMPLETIONS:** F17r is the ONLY page analyzed across three quires that contains NO `daiin`/`dain`/`daim` completion markers. Every other folio has at least 3. This means the procedure described on f17r is OPEN-ENDED — it does not complete. It is a PREPARATION page, setting up materials for subsequent use, or a CONTINUOUS PROCESS that runs without discrete checkpoints.

**-OM VESSEL SATURATION (5 terminals):** Five words end in `-om`: `chom`, `okchom`, `tchom`, `som`, `chotom`. The `-om` suffix (heat-vessel) marks products that are STORED IN VESSELS. This page is filling vessels — packing preparations into containers.

**-AM UNION SATURATION (4 terminals):** Four union markers: `daram` (fix-root-union-vessel), `qodam` (retort-heat-fix-union-vessel), `ypaim` (moist-press-complete-vessel), `chypcham` (volatile-active-press-volatile-union-vessel). Every union is COMPOUND — not simple unions but complex multi-step unions. Materials are being COMBINED in sophisticated ways.

**FSHODY (first word):** f-sh-o-dy = fire-transition-heat-fixed. The QUIRE OPENS WITH FIRE transitioning to fixed product. Quire A opened with `fachys` (fire-volatile), Quire B with `tydlo` (energy-fix-lock-heat). Each quire opener escalates: fire-volatile → energy-locked → fire-transitioned-to-fixed.

**QOF (P6):** Retort-fire — fire APPLIED INSIDE THE RETORT. Not fire heating the retort externally but fire WITHIN the sealed vessel. This is CALCINATION — burning material inside a sealed container.

## Process Summary

F17r describes **OPEN-ENDED VESSEL-PACKING WITH COMPOUND UNIONS AND CALCINATION** — materials prepared through fire-calcination (qof), combined in compound unions (4× -am), and packed into vessels (5× -om), all without discrete completion checkpoints. A staging/preparation page for Quire C.

### What Makes F17V Unique

**23 LINES — LONGEST PAGE:** F17v is the longest page in the first three quires. For comparison: f6v (21 lines), f8v (17 lines), f17v (23 lines). This is an EXTENDED PROCEDURE requiring elaborately detailed instruction. Buckwheat processing apparently demands meticulous multi-step work.

**ESSENCE-FLUID DOMINANCE:** The page is flooded with `-eol` (essence-heat-fluid), `-eey` (essence-active), `-eeor` (essence-heat-source) forms. Nearly every line contains at least one essence-marker. The entire procedure is oriented toward CAPTURING ESSENCE IN FLUID FORM. This is distillation of essential oils or extraction of aromatic compounds.

**QOKEEE (P22):** Retort-contain-triple-essence — the essence has been CONCENTRATED THREE TIMES inside the retort and then contained. Near the end of the page, after 20+ lines of processing, the triple-concentrated essence is finally captured.

**OLDAIM.ODAIIN.OKAL.OLDAIIN (P3):** Four consecutive tokens all beginning with `o-` (heat) — a HEAT CHAIN. Four heated operations in sequence without interruption. The material is CONTINUOUSLY HEATED through four distinct transformations.

**OTEOLOJ (P16):** The `-oj` terminal is extremely rare, appearing only a few times in the MS. It may represent a variant scribal formation or a distinct morpheme.

## Process Summary

F17v describes **EXTENDED ESSENCE-FLUID DISTILLATION** over 23 lines — the longest procedure in three quires. Essence captured in fluid through continuous heat chains, fire-sealed (fchol), and culminating in triple-concentrated retort essence (qokeee). An exhaustive essential-oil extraction protocol.

# FOLIO F18R — RECTO

## Identity & Botanical

## EVA Transcription

```
P1:  pdrairdy.darod*.yoar.ykchol.dor.om.chckhy.o*or.dyl-
P2:  otshol.qokchol.chykchy.okchal.daiin.dy.chol.dain-
P3:  qokchor.chor.chckhy.or.chey.qokchol.dy.ytcharg-
P4:  chor.cthor.okeor.ykchol.okain=

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix/Feature | Count | Significance |
|--------|-------|-------------|
| **-al terminals** | **6** (cthal, okchal, chlol, cthal, okal ×2) | **Structural building dominant** |
| **dar.dar.dal** (P6) | unique | **Triple fix-source/structure in sequence** |
| **ckh-** | 3 | Elevated valve control |
| **Title line** (T14) | 1 | Label present |
| **-g terminal** (P3, P10) | 2 | Rare terminal marker |
| **.om** (P1, P5) | 2 | Vessel terminals |

### What Makes F18R Unique

**DAR.DAR.DAL (P6):** Three consecutive d-prefix structural tokens — fix-root, fix-root, fix-structure. The ROOT IS FIXED TWICE, then the STRUCTURE is locked. A triple-anchoring sequence that pins the material at its source and then freezes its form. Alpine plants need deep anchoring (literally and procedurally).

**STRUCTURAL -AL CLUSTER (6 occurrences):** Six structure terminals across 13 lines — nearly one every other line. The page builds STRUCTURAL SCAFFOLDING throughout the procedure. Every few steps, a structural lock is applied.

**TWO-PARAGRAPH + TITLE:** P1-P4 (first paragraph), P5-P12 (second paragraph), T14 (title/label). The first paragraph EXTRACTS, the second paragraph BUILDS STRUCTURE, and the title NAMES the product. Clear three-phase architecture.

**-G TERMINALS (P3, P10):** Two words ending in `-g` (`ytcharg`, `g`). This rare terminal appears more in Quire C than A or B combined. It may be a scribal flourish, abbreviation marker, or a distinct phonetic element.

## Process Summary

F18r describes **STRUCTURAL SCAFFOLDING WITH TRIPLE ROOT-ANCHORING** — alpine aster material extracted, then built into structural form through 6 structure-locks and the unique dar.dar.dal triple-anchoring sequence. Two-phase procedure with a product label.

# FOLIO F18V — VERSO

## Identity & Botanical

| Property | Value |

## EVA Transcription

```
P1:  told.shor.ytshy.otchdal.dchal.dchy.ytchm-
P2:  qoeees.or.oaiin.shy*.okshy.qokchy.qokchy.s.g-
P3:  or*shy.qoky.qoky.chkchy.qokshy.qokam-
P4:  qotchy.qokay.qokchy.ykcho.ydl.dan-
P5:  ychoees.ykchy.qol.kchy.qotchol.dair.om-
P6:  qotor.chor.otchy.qokeees.chy.s.ar.ykar-
P7:  ychol.dor.chod.qokol.daiin.qotol.dar.dy-
P8:  tolol.sh.cphoy.daror.ddy.ytor.ykam-
P9:  okchor.qotchy.qokchy.ytol.doky.dy-
P10: !!!!!!!yko!!!!!!!!!!.dysh!!!!!!!.dair.ykol.dom=
```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix/Feature | Count | Significance |
|--------|-------|-------------|
| **qo-** | **12** | **EXTREME retort — 12 in 10 lines** |
| **qoeees** (P2) | 1 | Retort-triple-essence |
| **qokeees** (P6) | 1 | **Retort-contain-triple-essence** |
| **qokam** (P3) | 1 | Retort-contain-union-vessel |
| **ykam** (P8) | 1 | Active-contain-union-vessel |
| **ddy** (P8) | 1 | Double-fix (cf. f11v) |
| **tolol** (P8) | 1 | Energy-fluid-heat-fluid |
| **DAMAGE** | P10 | Physical damage — text partially lost |

### What Makes F18V Unique

**DOUBLE TRIPLE-ESSENCE (qoeees + qokeees):** Two retort-triple-essence tokens on the same page — the retort processes TRIPLE-CONCENTRATED ESSENCE, then CONTAINS IT and processes it AGAIN. Double-pass triple-concentration. The most aggressive essence-concentration protocol seen yet.

**QO- SATURATION (12 in 10 lines):** 1.2 retort tokens per line — wall-to-wall retort cycling. Lines P2-P6 each contain 2-3 qo- tokens. The retort is running CONTINUOUSLY, not in discrete batches.

**QOKAM (P3):** Retort-contain-union-vessel. The union happens INSIDE THE RETORT VESSEL. Materials are being COMBINED DURING RETORT CYCLING — not mixed before or after, but united while being distilled. This is CO-DISTILLATION.

**PHYSICAL DAMAGE (P10):** The `!!!!` marks indicate ink blots or physical damage to the manuscript. The underlying text is partially illegible. What survives (`yko...dysh...dair.ykol.dom`) suggests a standard fixation-vessel closing, but critical intermediate tokens are lost.

**TOLD (first word):** t-o-l-d = energy-heat-lock-fix. The page begins with ENERGY-LOCKED FIXATION — material already in a locked state before processing begins. This is a CONTINUATION procedure — the material was prepared earlier (f18r?) and is now being further processed.

## Process Summary

F18v describes **CONTINUOUS CO-DISTILLATION WITH DOUBLE TRIPLE-ESSENCE CONCENTRATION** — retort runs continuously (12 qo- in 10 lines), processing triple-concentrated essence twice (qoeees + qokeees), with materials co-distilled inside the retort vessel (qokam). Partially damaged text obscures the closing sequence.

### What Makes F19R Unique

**11 COMPLETIONS IN 13 LINES:** Almost one completion per line — the most verified page in Quire C. Greek valerian (sedative herb) demands EXTREME VERIFICATION at every step. Medicinal dosage control requires constant checkpoint confirmation.

**DAIINOL (P12):** daiin-ol = completion-fluid. The completion marker is FUSED WITH THE FLUID SUFFIX. The product is complete AS A FLUID. Not fixed and stored, but complete in its liquid state. A tincture or liquid sedative.

**QOKORAR (P4):** qo-k-or-ar = retort-contain-source-root. The retort reaches down to the SOURCE ROOT of the material. Deep extraction from the root system through retort processing.

**SHDAIIN (P9):** sh-d-aiin = transition-fix-completion. Completion is achieved THROUGH TRANSITION — the act of changing phase IS the completion event. The transformation itself is the goal.

**SHORT LINES (P5: 5 tokens, P6: 5 tokens):** The middle of the page contracts to very short lines — rapid-fire completion checks. Brief, emphatic verifications between longer operational passages.

## Process Summary

F19r describes **HYPER-VERIFIED SEDATIVE TINCTURE PREPARATION** — 11 completions in 13 lines, producing a fluid product (daiinol), with deep root extraction (qokorar) and completion-through-transition (shdaiin). Every step of the sedative preparation is individually verified.

### What Makes F19V Unique

**DDOR (P8):** Double-d source-marker. The fixation is DOUBLED AT THE SOURCE — the root material is fixed twice before any further processing. Compare f11v's `ddy` (double-fix-active) — both are double-d formations but ddor anchors to the SOURCE while ddy remains ACTIVE.

**DAIIN.DAIIN (P4):** Two consecutive completion markers — the procedure pauses for DOUBLE VERIFICATION before proceeding. This is a HOLD-AND-CONFIRM point.

**OTCHOLCHEAIIN (T13):** The title-line token is a MEGA-COMPOUND: ot-ch-ol-ch-e-aiin = heat-energy-volatile-fluid-volatile-essence-complete. The product name ENCODES ITS ENTIRE PROCESS — heated volatile fluid with volatile essence, completed. The title IS the recipe in miniature.

**Y-PREFIX CHAIN (P12):** `yees.ykchol.oty.ytor.ytar.ytchor.ytaiin` — SIX consecutive y-prefix tokens. The final operational line is entirely MOIST/ACTIVE processing. The procedure ends in a WET ACTIVE STATE.

## Process Summary

F19v describes **DOUBLE-VERIFIED ALPINE EXTRACTION WITH LACUNA** — doubled completions (daiin.daiin), doubled source-fixation (ddor), a text gap (missing P6), and a mega-compound product label (otcholcheaiin). Ends in wet active processing.

Quire C's center holds essence-extraction (f20r) and fire-transition (f20v/f21r). The center position may be THEMATICALLY SIGNIFICANT — the core technique of each quire.

## Process Summary

F20r describes **THREE-PHASE ESSENCE EXTRACTION WITH FIRE-COMPOUND CATALYSIS** — center-bifolio page with saturated essence markers, a 6-morpheme fire-compound (fchodees), and clear three-paragraph sectioning. The core technique of Quire C: essence capture.

### What Makes F20V Unique

Each fire token is a COMPOUND — fire is never simple on this page, always combined with other operations. This is COMPLEX FIRE MANAGEMENT — artichoke/cardoon processed through four different fire applications.

**TRANSITION SATURATION (sh-/sho- = 12):** Twelve transition/infusion markers — the highest in Quire C. The procedure is dominated by SOAKING, STEEPING, and TRANSITIONING material between states. Artichoke hearts are traditionally processed by extended soaking/cooking.

**FAIIS (first word):** f-aiin-s = fire-complete-salt. The page opens with FIRE COMPLETING A SALT. A salt product is MADE BY FIRE as the first operation. This may encode ash-production — burning plant material to produce medicinal salts (a standard alchemical/pharmaceutical technique).

**CHORALY (P8):** ch-or-al-y = volatile-source-structure-active. An unusual formation with structural intent — the volatile is being given ACTIVE STRUCTURE at its source. Building form from vapor.

## Process Summary

F20v describes **COMPLEX FIRE-MANAGED SOAKING/INFUSION OF ARTICHOKE** — four compound fire operations, maximum transition density (12 sh-/sho-), fire-salt opening (faiis), and triple-i fixation (doiiin). The center bifolio's verso focuses on FIRE + SOAKING as combined technique.

## Quantitative Profile

### What Makes F21V Unique

This matches f7r's `deeeese` (quintuple-e) as the most intensified essence marker in the manuscript. Burning bush (*Dictamnus albus*) produces volatile oils so concentrated they can spontaneously ignite — the quintuple essence marker encodes this EXTREME CONCENTRATION.

**OEEESOY (P2):** Triple-essence before the quintuple-essence — the page ESCALATES from triple (3×) to quintuple (5×). Progressive concentration: 3→5. This is STAGED CONCENTRATION — essence is concentrated in steps.

**FIRE-INSIDE-RETORT (qofshey, chofchy):** Two tokens with fire EMBEDDED inside volatile/retort operations. The fire is CONTAINED WITHIN THE VOLATILE MEDIUM — appropriate for a plant whose volatile oils are literally flammable. The text mirrors the plant's physical property.

**SHORT PAGE (8 lines):** Like f5r's short lethal procedure, brevity here signals DANGER — concentrated volatile flammable oils require brief, precise handling. Get in, get the quintuple essence, get out.

**DAIIN.DAIIN (P4) + TODAIIN.DAIIN (P6):** Two instances of doubled-completion. The procedure double-checks TWICE — four total verification events in two pairs. Extreme caution.

## Process Summary

F21v describes **QUINTUPLE-ESSENCE EXTRACTION FROM FLAMMABLE VOLATILE OIL** — staged concentration (triple→quintuple), fire contained inside volatile medium (qofshey, chofchy), brief precise handling (8 lines), and quadruple verification (2× doubled completions). The center bifolio's final page encodes the quire's most concentrated — and most flammable — product.

```
P1:  pol.olshy.fcholy.shol.dpchy.oty.okoly.daiin.opchy.s.ocphy-
P2:  ol.aiin.shol.o.kor.qokchol.daiin.okaiin.cthor.dain.ckhy.dom-

P13: dchor.dy.dain.qockhy.ykol.okain=
```

## Quantitative Profile

| Prefix/Feature | Count | Significance |
|--------|-------|-------------|
| **daiin/dain** | **13** | **MAXIMUM COMPLETIONS IN QUIRE C** |
| **cfhy** (P4) | 1 | **Fire seal variant — cfh-active** |
| **fcholy** (P1) | 1 | Fire-volatile-heat-lock-active |
| **dom** (P2) | 1 | Vessel terminal |
| **oldam** (P10) | 1 | Fluid-fix-union-vessel |
| **shain** (P3) | 1 | Transition-complete |
| **3 paragraphs** | P1-3, P4-6, P7-13 | Three-section |

### What Makes F22R Unique

**13 COMPLETIONS — QUIRE C MAXIMUM:** Thirteen `daiin`/`dain` markers in 13 lines — exactly ONE PER LINE on average. Every single line is checkpoint-verified. Vervain was one of the most sacred herbs in European medicine — its preparation demanded maximum ritual precision.

**CFHY (P4):** A FIRE SEAL VARIANT — `cfh-y` (fire-seal-active). The fire seal is rendered ACTIVE, not just containment but active fire-sealed processing. Compare `cfhol` (fire-seal-fluid) from earlier quires — this variant is DRY and ACTIVE rather than wet and contained.

**OLDAM (P10):** ol-d-am = fluid-fix-union-vessel. The fluid product is FIXED, then UNITED IN A VESSEL. A combination preparation — vervain combined with another ingredient in the final vessel.

**DAIIN.YDAIIN (P12):** Standard completion followed by moist-completion — the product is verified dry, then verified wet. DUAL-STATE VERIFICATION — ensuring the product works in both dry and moist forms.

**THREE PARAGRAPHS EXPANDING:** P1-3 (short), P4-6 (shorter), P7-13 (long). The sections GROW — brief setup, briefer transition, extended main procedure. Funnel-shaped architecture.

## Process Summary

F22r describes **RITUALLY PRECISE SACRED HERB PREPARATION WITH ACTIVE FIRE SEAL** — maximum Quire C completions (13), active fire seal (cfhy), dual-state verification (daiin.ydaiin), and expanding three-section architecture. The most verified page in Quire C.

### What Makes F22V Unique

**DALDALOL (T16, title line):** dal-dal-ol = DOUBLED STRUCTURAL FIXATION + FLUID. The product label contains a DOUBLED STRUCTURE — the final product has its structure FIXED TWICE and exists as a fluid. A structurally reinforced liquid preparation. This doubled structural morpheme is unique in the corpus.

**CONTRACTING LINE LENGTHS:** Lines progressively shorten from P1 (8 tokens) through to P11-12 (3 tokens each), then slightly expand for the close. The procedure WINDS DOWN — operations become briefer and simpler as the product approaches completion. A convergent architecture.

**POSAIINOR (P1, first word):** p-o-s-aiin-or = press-heat-salt-complete-source. The opening word contains a COMPLETION MARKER INSIDE IT. The process begins with a salt operation that is ALREADY COMPLETE — this is a continuation from a previous preparation.

**SAIINCHY (T16, title):** Salt-completion-volatile-active. The product title identifies it as a SALT-COMPLETED VOLATILE — an active volatile preparation that has undergone salt processing. A salted aromatic from tulip bulbs.

## Process Summary

F22v describes **CONVERGING SALT-VOLATILE PREPARATION WITH DOUBLED STRUCTURAL PRODUCT** — contracting line architecture, salt-complete opener (posaiinor), doubled structural product label (daldalol), and progressive simplification toward completion. A tulip-bulb salted aromatic.

### What Makes F23R Unique

**FCHOLDY (P1) + OFCHOL (P4) + YFCHOR (P4) + OLFCHOR (P4):** FOUR TOTAL fire-seal/fire-volatile tokens plus `pydchdom` opening. This is the most FIRE-SEAL-INTENSIVE page in the entire manuscript. The toxic compound is being sealed repeatedly under fire conditions.

**7× -DAL STRUCTURE:** Seven structural fixation terminals — the structure is being BUILT AND REBUILT throughout. The toxic preparation demands extreme structural integrity to contain the active compound.

**LONG DENSE LINES:** P1 has 11 tokens, P4 has 10 — among the longest lines in three quires. Dense, packed instruction for a dangerous procedure.

## Process Summary

F23r describes **TRIPLE-FIRE-SEALED TOXIC COMPOUND PREPARATION** — most fire-seal-intensive page in the manuscript, with three fire-seal variants in one line (ofchol, yfchor, olfchor), triple union (dam×2 + alm), extreme structural fixation (7× -dal), and dense packed instruction. Pasque flower's toxin handled with maximum containment.

### What Makes F23V Unique

**OL- FLUID SATURATION (~12 tokens):** Nearly every line contains multiple `ol` (fluid) markers. This is the most FLUID-INTENSIVE page in three quires. The product exists entirely in liquid form — the preparation IS the fluid.

**EEEOLY (P12, final word):** eee-ol-y = triple-essence-fluid-active. The page (and the bifolio) CLOSES with an active triple-essence fluid. This is the PRODUCT — a concentrated borage oil or tincture.

**DOUBLE OLOL + SHOLOL:** Two doubled-fluid formations. The fluid is DOUBLED — either the quantity is doubled, or the fluid is processed twice through the same extraction.

**DAM.CHOR.OLOL.DAM (P8):** Union-volatile-doubled fluid-union. Two unions BRACKETING a doubled volatile fluid. The volatile fluid is UNITED on both sides — combined with ingredients before and after.

**SOL.DAIIN (P7):** Salt-fluid followed by completion. A salt-in-fluid product (saline tincture) verified as complete. Borage was traditionally prepared as a salted decoction.

## Process Summary
